Although of considerable selenological interest, this insight does not mean that water is easily available since the sample originated many kilometers below the surface, and the inclusions are so difficult to access that it took 39 years to find them with a state-of-the-art ion microprobe instrument.

Analysis of the findings of the Moon Mineralogy Mapper (M3) revealed in August 2018 for the first time "definitive evidence" for water-ice on the lunar surface.[[173]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-:1-181)[[174]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-182) The data revealed the distinct reflective signatures of water-ice, as opposed to dust and other reflective substances.[[175]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-:2-183) The ice deposits were found on the North and South poles, although it is more abundant in the South, where water is trapped in permanently shadowed craters and crevices, allowing it to persist as ice on the surface since they are shielded from the sun.[[173]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-:1-181)[[175]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-:2-183)

In October 2020, astronomers reported detecting [molecular water](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water "Water") on the sunlit surface of the Moon by several independent spacecraft, including the [Stratospheric Observatory for Infrared Astronomy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stratospheric_Observatory_for_Infrared_Astronomy "Stratospheric Observatory for Infrared Astronomy") (SOFIA).[[176]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-NA-20201026-184)[[177]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-NA-20201026poh-185)[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-WP-20201026-186)[[179]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-NYT-20201026-187)

Earth‚ÄìMoon system
-----------------

### Orbit

[![Image 26](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Dscovrepicmoontransitfull.gif/250px-Dscovrepicmoontransitfull.gif)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Dscovrepicmoontransitfull.gif)

A view of the rotating Earth and the [far side of the Moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Far_side_of_the_Moon "Far side of the Moon") as the Moon passes on its orbit in between the observing [DSCOVR satellite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DSCOVR_satellite "DSCOVR satellite") and Earth

The Earth and the Moon form the Earth‚ÄìMoon [satellite system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Satellite_system_(astronomy) "Satellite system (astronomy)") with a shared center of mass, or [barycenter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barycenter "Barycenter"). This barycenter is 1,700 km (1,100 mi) (about a quarter of Earth's radius) beneath the Earth's surface.

The Moon's orbit is slightly elliptical, with an [orbital eccentricity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orbital_eccentricity "Orbital eccentricity") of 0.055.[[1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-W06-1) The [semi-major axis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semi-major_axis "Semi-major axis") of the geocentric lunar orbit, called the [lunar distance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_distance "Lunar distance"), is approximately 400,000 km (250,000 miles or 1.28 light-seconds), comparable to going [around Earth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Circumference_of_Earth "Circumference of Earth") 9.5 times.[[180]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-The_Aerospace_Corporation_2023_j509-188)

The Moon makes a complete orbit around Earth with respect to the fixed stars, its [sidereal period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sidereal_period "Sidereal period"), about once every 27.3 days.[[i]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-orbpd-189) However, because the Earth‚ÄìMoon system moves at the same time in its orbit around the Sun, it takes slightly longer, 29.5 days,[[j]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-synpd-190)[[70]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-worldbook-78) to return to the same [lunar phase](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_phase "Lunar phase"),[[181]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-191) completing a full cycle, as seen from Earth. This [synodic period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synodic_period "Synodic period") or synodic month is commonly known as the [lunar month](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_month "Lunar month") and is equal to the length of the [solar day](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_day "Solar day") on the Moon.[[182]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Day-192)

Due to [tidal locking](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tidal_locking "Tidal locking"), the Moon has a 1:1 [spin‚Äìorbit resonance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orbital_resonance "Orbital resonance"). This [rotation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rotation "Rotation")‚Äì[orbit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orbit "Orbit") ratio makes the Moon's orbital periods around Earth equal to its corresponding [rotation periods](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rotation_period "Rotation period"). This is the reason for only one side of the Moon, its so-called [near side](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Near_side "Near side"), being visible from Earth. That said, while the movement of the Moon is in resonance, it still is not without nuances such as [libration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Libration "Libration"), resulting in slightly changing perspectives, making over time and location on Earth about 59% of the Moon's surface visible from Earth.[[183]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Liberation-193)

Unlike most satellites of other planets, the Moon's orbital plane is closer to the [ecliptic plane](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecliptic_plane "Ecliptic plane") than to the planet's [equatorial plane](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equatorial_plane "Equatorial plane"). The Moon's orbit is subtly [perturbed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perturbation_(astronomy) "Perturbation (astronomy)") by the Sun and Earth in many small, complex and interacting ways. For example, the plane of the Moon's orbit [gradually rotates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_standstill "Lunar standstill") once every 18.61 years,[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-194) which affects other aspects of lunar motion. These follow-on effects are mathematically described by [Cassini's laws](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cassini%27s_laws "Cassini's laws").[[185]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Beletskii2-195)

[![Image 27](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Moon_distance_range_to_scale.svg/750px-Moon_distance_range_to_scale.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Moon_distance_range_to_scale.svg)

Minimum, mean and maximum distances of the Moon from Earth with its angular diameter as seen from Earth's surface to scale

### Tidal effects

[![Image 28](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Tide_animation.gif/250px-Tide_animation.gif)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Tide_animation.gif)

Simplified diagram of Earth bulging, being pulled and stretched toward the Moon by its gravity, which is the main driver of the [tides](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tide "Tide"). The Ocean and Earth are being pulled more where it is closer to the Moon, causing [tidal forces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tidal_force "Tidal force") to be weaker at the far-side of Earth creating a second bulge and high-tide. The animation shows the change of the Moon's position on its inclined orbit.

The gravitational attraction that Earth and the Moon (as well as the Sun) exert on each other manifests in a slightly greater attraction on the sides closest to each other, resulting in [tidal forces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tidal_forces "Tidal forces"). [Ocean tides](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ocean_tides "Ocean tides") are the most widely experienced result of this, but tidal forces also considerably affect other mechanics of Earth, as well as the Moon and their system.

The lunar solid crust experiences tides of around 10 cm (4 in) amplitude over 27 days, with three components: a fixed one due to Earth, because they are in [synchronous rotation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synchronous_rotation "Synchronous rotation"), a variable tide due to orbital eccentricity and inclination, and a small varying component from the Sun.[[186]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-touma1994-196) The Earth-induced variable component arises from changing distance and [libration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Libration "Libration"), a result of the Moon's orbital eccentricity and inclination (if the Moon's orbit were perfectly circular and un-inclined, there would only be solar tides).[[186]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-touma1994-196) According to recent research, scientists suggest that the Moon's influence on the Earth may contribute to maintaining [Earth's magnetic field](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth%27s_magnetic_field "Earth's magnetic field").[[187]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-197)

The cumulative effects of stress built up by these tidal forces produces [moonquakes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moonquakes "Moonquakes"). Moonquakes are much less common and weaker than are earthquakes, although moonquakes can last for up to an hour‚Äì significantly longer than terrestrial quakes‚Äì because of scattering of the seismic vibrations in the dry fragmented upper crust. The existence of moonquakes was an unexpected discovery from [seismometers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seismometer "Seismometer") placed on the Moon by [Apollo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_program "Apollo program")[astronauts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astronaut "Astronaut") from 1969 through 1972.[[188]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-198)

The most commonly known effect of tidal forces is elevated sea levels called ocean tides.[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Lambeck1977-199) While the Moon exerts most of the tidal forces, the Sun also exerts tidal forces and therefore contributes to the tides as much as 40% of the Moon's tidal force; producing in interplay the [spring and neap tides](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spring_tide "Spring tide").[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Lambeck1977-199)

The tides are two bulges in the Earth's oceans, one on the side facing the Moon and the other on the side opposite. As the Earth rotates on its axis, one of the ocean bulges (high tide) is held in place "under" the Moon, while another such tide is opposite. The tide under the Moon is explained by the Moon's gravity being stronger on the water close to it. The tide on the opposite side can be explained either by the centrifugal force as the Earth orbits the [barycenter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barycenter "Barycenter") or by the water's inertia as the Moon's gravity is stronger on the solid Earth close to it and it is pulled away from the farther water.[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-200)[[191]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-201)

Thus, there are two high tides, and two low tides in about 24 hours.[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Lambeck1977-199) Since the Moon is orbiting the Earth in the same direction of the Earth's rotation, the high tides occur about every 12 hours and 25 minutes; the 25 minutes is due to the Moon's time to orbit the Earth.

If the Earth were a water world (one with no continents) it would produce a tide of only one meter, and that tide would be very predictable, but the ocean tides are greatly modified by other effects:

*   the frictional coupling of water to Earth's rotation through the ocean floors
*   the [inertia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inertia "Inertia") of water's movement
*   ocean basins that grow shallower near land
*   the sloshing of water between different ocean basins[[192]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-202)

As a result, the timing of the tides at most points on the Earth is a product of observations that are explained, incidentally, by theory.

#### System evolution

Delays in the tidal peaks of both ocean and solid-body tides cause [torque](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Torque "Torque") in opposition to the Earth's rotation. This "drains" [angular momentum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Angular_momentum "Angular momentum") and rotational [kinetic energy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kinetic_energy "Kinetic energy") from Earth's rotation, slowing the Earth's rotation.[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Lambeck1977-199)[[186]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-touma1994-196) That angular momentum, lost from the Earth, is transferred to the Moon in a process known as [tidal acceleration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tidal_acceleration "Tidal acceleration"), which lifts the Moon into a higher orbit while lowering orbital speed around the Earth. This has resulted in the length of a [anomalistic month](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anomalistic_month "Anomalistic month") having increased from 20 days to today's 27.55 days over the course of 3.2 billion years.[[193]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-m870-203)

Thus the distance between Earth and Moon is increasing, and the Earth's rotation is slowing in reaction.[[186]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-touma1994-196) Measurements from laser reflectors left during the Apollo missions ([lunar ranging experiments](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_Laser_Ranging_experiments "Lunar Laser Ranging experiments")) have found that the Moon's distance increases by 38 mm (1.5 in) per year (roughly the rate at which human fingernails grow).[[194]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-204)[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-205)[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-206)[Atomic clocks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atomic_clock "Atomic clock") show that Earth's Day lengthens by about 17[microseconds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microsecond "Microsecond") every year,[[197]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-207)[[198]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-208)[[199]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-209) slowly increasing the rate at which [UTC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UTC "UTC") is adjusted by [leap seconds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leap_second "Leap second").

This tidal drag makes the rotation of the Earth, and the orbital period of the Moon very slowly match. This matching first results in [tidally locking](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tidal_locking "Tidal locking") the lighter body of the orbital system, as is already the case with the Moon. Theoretically, in 50 billion years,[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Universe_Today_2016-210) the Earth's rotation will have slowed to the point of matching the Moon's orbital period, causing the Earth to always present the same side to the Moon. However, the Sun will become a [red giant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_giant#The_Sun_as_a_red_giant "Red giant"), most likely engulfing the Earth‚ÄìMoon system long before then.[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-211)[[202]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-212)

If the Earth‚ÄìMoon system isn't engulfed by the enlarged Sun, the drag from the solar atmosphere can cause the orbit of the Moon to decay. Once the orbit of the Moon closes to a distance of 18,470 km (11,480 mi), it will cross Earth's [Roche limit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roche_limit "Roche limit"), meaning that tidal interaction with Earth would break apart the Moon, turning it into a [ring system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ring_system "Ring system"). Most of the orbiting rings will begin to decay, and the debris will impact Earth. Hence, even if the Sun does not swallow up Earth, the planet may be left moonless.[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-space070122-213)

Orientation and appearance
--------------------------

[![Image 29: Over one lunar month more than half of the Moon's surface can be seen from Earth's surface.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Lunar_libration_with_phase_Oct_2007_HD.gif/250px-Lunar_libration_with_phase_Oct_2007_HD.gif)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lunar_libration_with_phase_Oct_2007_HD.gif)

[Libration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Libration "Libration"), the slight variation in the Moon's [apparent size](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apparent_size "Apparent size") and viewing angle over a single lunar month as viewed from somewhere on the Earth's northern hemisphere.

The Moon appears in Earth's sky differently depending on the position of observation on Earth and the time of [lunar year](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_year "Lunar year"), [lunar month](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_month "Lunar month") and day on Earth. During a year the Moon [culminates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culmination "Culmination") during a day at different [altitudes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Altitude_(astronomy) "Altitude (astronomy)"). The Moon appears highest in the sky unlike the Sun during winter and lowest during summer, which is true for the seasons of each of Earth's northern and southern hemispheres.

At the [North](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Pole "North Pole") and [South Poles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Pole "South Pole") the Moon is 24 hours above the horizon for two weeks every [tropical month](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_month "Tropical month") (about 27.3 days), comparable to the [polar day](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polar_day "Polar day") of the [tropical year](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_year "Tropical year"). [Zooplankton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zooplankton "Zooplankton") in the [Arctic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arctic "Arctic") use [moonlight](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moonlight "Moonlight") when the Sun is [below the horizon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polar_night "Polar night") for months on end.[[204]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-214)

The apparent orientation of the Moon depends on its position in the sky and the hemisphere of the Earth from which it is being viewed. In the [northern hemisphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_hemisphere "Northern hemisphere") it appears upside down compared to the view from the [southern hemisphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_hemisphere "Southern hemisphere").[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-215) Sometimes the "horns" of a crescent moon appear to be pointing more upwards than sideways. This phenomenon is called a [wet moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wet_moon "Wet moon") and occurs more frequently in the [tropics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropics "Tropics").[[206]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-216)

The [distance between the Moon and Earth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_distance "Lunar distance") varies from around 356,400 km (221,500 mi) ([perigee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perigee "Perigee")) to 406,700 km (252,700 mi) (apogee), making the Moon's distance and apparent size fluctuate up to 14%.[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-size1-217)[[208]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-size2-218) On average the Moon's [angular diameter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Angular_diameter "Angular diameter") is about 0.52¬∞, roughly the same apparent size as the Sun (see [¬ßEclipses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#Eclipses)). In addition, a purely psychological effect, known as the [Moon illusion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon_illusion "Moon illusion"), makes the Moon appear larger when close to the horizon.[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-219)

### Rotation

[![Image 30](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Tidal_locking_of_the_Moon_with_the_Earth.gif/250px-Tidal_locking_of_the_Moon_with_the_Earth.gif)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Tidal_locking_of_the_Moon_with_the_Earth.gif)

Comparison between the Moon on the left, rotating tidally locked (correct), and with the Moon on the right, without rotation (incorrect)

The [tidally locked synchronous rotation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synchronous_rotation "Synchronous rotation") of the Moon as it orbits the Earth results in it always keeping nearly the same face turned towards the planet. The side of the Moon that faces Earth is called the [near side](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Near_side "Near side"), and the opposite the [far side](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Far_side_of_the_Moon "Far side of the Moon"). The far side is often inaccurately called the "dark side", but it is in fact illuminated as often as the near side: once every 29.5 Earth days. During [dark moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dark_moon "Dark moon") to [new moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_moon "New moon"), the near side is dark.[[210]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-220)

The Moon originally rotated at a faster rate, but early in its history its rotation slowed and became [tidally locked](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tidally_locked "Tidally locked") in this orientation as a result of [frictional](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friction "Friction") effects associated with [tidal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tidal_force "Tidal force") deformations caused by Earth.[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-221) With time, the energy of rotation of the Moon on its axis was dissipated as heat, until there was no rotation of the Moon relative to Earth. In 2016, planetary scientists using data collected on the 1998‚Äì99 NASA _[Lunar Prospector](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar\_Prospector "Lunar Prospector")_ mission found two hydrogen-rich areas (most likely former water ice) on opposite sides of the Moon. It is speculated that these patches were the poles of the Moon billions of years ago before it was tidally locked to Earth.[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-222)

### Illumination and phases

[![Image 31](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Moon_phases_en.jpg/960px-Moon_phases_en.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Moon_phases_en.jpg)

The monthly changes in the angle between the direction of sunlight and view from Earth, and the [phases of the Moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_phase "Lunar phase") that result, as viewed from the [Northern Hemisphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere "Northern Hemisphere"). The [Earth‚ÄìMoon distance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth%E2%80%93Moon_distance "Earth‚ÄìMoon distance") is not to scale.

The Moon rotates, as it orbits Earth, changing orientation toward the Sun, experiencing a [lunar day](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_day "Lunar day"). A lunar day is equal to one [lunar month](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_month "Lunar month") (one synodic orbit around Earth) due to it being [tidally locked](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tidal_locking "Tidal locking") to Earth. Since the Moon is not tidally locked to the Sun, lunar daylight and night times both occur around the Moon. The changing position of the illumination of the Moon by the Sun during a lunar day is observable from Earth as the changing [lunar phases](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_phase "Lunar phase"), waxing crescent being the sunrise and the waning crescent the sunset phase of a day observed from afar.[[213]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-r040-223)

Lunar night is the darkest on the far side and during lunar eclipses on the near side (and darker than a moonless night on Earth). The near side is during its night illuminated by [Earthlight](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earthlight "Earthlight"), making the near side illuminated enough by the Earthlight to see lunar surface features from Earth where it is dark during its night phase due to Earthlight being reflected back to Earth. Earthshine makes the night on the near side about 43 times brighter, and sometimes even 55 times brighter than a night on Earth illuminated by the light of the full moon.[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-u988-224)

In Earth's sky brightness and apparent size of the Moon changes also due to its elliptic [orbit around Earth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orbit_of_the_Moon "Orbit of the Moon"). At [perigee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perigee "Perigee") (closest), since the Moon is up to 14% closer to Earth than at [apogee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apogee "Apogee") (most distant), it subtends a [solid angle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solid_angle "Solid angle") which is up to 30% larger. Consequently, given the same phase, the Moon's brightness also varies by up to 30% between apogee and perigee.[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-225) A full (or new) moon at such a position is called a [supermoon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supermoon "Supermoon").[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-size1-217)[[208]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-size2-218)[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-226)

#### Observational phenomena

There has been historical controversy over whether observed features on the Moon's surface change over time. Today, many of these claims are thought to be illusory, resulting from observation under different lighting conditions, poor [astronomical seeing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astronomical_seeing "Astronomical seeing"), or inadequate drawings. However, [outgassing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Outgassing "Outgassing") does occasionally occur and could be responsible for a minor percentage of the reported [lunar transient phenomena](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_transient_phenomena "Lunar transient phenomena"). Recently, it has been suggested that a roughly 3 km (1.9 mi) diameter region of the lunar surface was modified by a gas release event about a million years ago.[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-227)[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-228)

### Albedo and color

[![Image 32](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Two_Lunar_Phases.jpg/250px-Two_Lunar_Phases.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Two_Lunar_Phases.jpg)

The changing apparent color of the Moon, filtered by Earth's atmosphere

The Moon has an exceptionally low [albedo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albedo "Albedo"), giving it a [reflectance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diffuse_reflection "Diffuse reflection") that is slightly brighter than that of worn [asphalt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asphalt_concrete "Asphalt concrete"). Despite this, it is the [brightest object in the sky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_brightest_natural_objects_in_the_sky "List of brightest natural objects in the sky") after the [Sun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sun "Sun").[[70]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-worldbook-78)[[k]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-brightness-229) This is due partly to the brightness enhancement of the [opposition surge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opposition_surge "Opposition surge"); the Moon at quarter phase is only one-tenth as bright, rather than half as bright, as at [full moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Full_moon "Full moon").[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Moon-230) Additionally, [color constancy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Color_constancy "Color constancy") in the [visual system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Visual_system "Visual system") recalibrates the relations between the colors of an object and its surroundings, and because the surrounding sky is comparatively dark, the sunlit Moon is perceived as a bright object. The edges of the full moon seem as bright as the center, without [limb darkening](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Limb_darkening "Limb darkening"), because of the [reflective properties](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lambert%27s_cosine_law#Lambertian_scatterers_and_radiators "Lambert's cosine law") of [lunar soil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_soil "Lunar soil"), which [retroreflects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Retroreflector "Retroreflector") light more towards the Sun than in other directions. The Moon's color depends on the light the Moon reflects, which in turn depends on the Moon's surface and its features, having for example large darker regions. In general, the lunar surface reflects a brown-tinged gray light.[[220]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Science_Mission_Directorate_2020-231)

At times, the Moon can appear red or blue. It may appear red during a [lunar eclipse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_eclipse "Lunar eclipse"), because of the red spectrum of the Sun's light being [refracted](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Refracted "Refracted") onto the Moon by Earth's atmosphere. Because of this red color, lunar eclipses are also sometimes called [blood moons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blood_Moon_(eclipse) "Blood Moon (eclipse)"). The Moon can also seem red when it appears at low angles and through a thick atmosphere.

The Moon may appear blue depending on the presence of certain particles in the air,[[220]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Science_Mission_Directorate_2020-231) such as volcanic particles,[[221]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-232) in which case it can be called a [blue moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blue_moon#Whole_blue_moon "Blue moon").

Because the words "red moon" and "blue moon" can also be used to refer to specific [full moons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Full_moon "Full moon") of the year, they do not always refer to the presence of red or blue [moonlight](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moonlight "Moonlight").

### Eclipses

[![Image 33](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Solar_eclipse_1999_4.jpg/250px-Solar_eclipse_1999_4.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Solar_eclipse_1999_4.jpg)

[![Image 34](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Full_Eclipse_of_the_Moon_as_seen_in_from_Irvine%2C_CA%2C_USA_%2852075715442%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Full_Eclipse_of_the_Moon_as_seen_in_from_Irvine%2C_CA%2C_USA_%2852075715442%29_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Full_Eclipse_of_the_Moon_as_seen_in_from_Irvine,_CA,_USA_(52075715442)_(cropped).jpg)

Eclipses only occur when the Sun, Earth, and Moon are all in a straight line (termed "[syzygy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syzygy_(astronomy) "Syzygy (astronomy)")"). [Solar eclipses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_eclipse "Solar eclipse") occur at [new moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_moon "New moon"), when the Moon is between the Sun and Earth. In contrast, [lunar eclipses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_eclipse "Lunar eclipse") occur at full moon, when Earth is between the Sun and Moon. The apparent size of the Moon is roughly the same as that of the Sun, with both being viewed at close to one-half a degree wide. The Sun is much larger than the Moon, but it is the vastly greater distance that gives it the same apparent size as the much closer and much smaller Moon from the perspective of Earth. The variations in apparent size, due to the non-circular orbits, are nearly the same as well, though occurring in different cycles. This makes possible both [total](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Total_eclipse "Total eclipse") (with the Moon appearing larger than the Sun) and [annular](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Annular_eclipse "Annular eclipse") (with the Moon appearing smaller than the Sun) solar eclipses.[[222]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-233) In a total eclipse, the Moon completely covers the disc of the Sun and the [solar corona](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_corona "Solar corona") becomes visible to the [naked eye](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naked_eye "Naked eye").

Because the distance between the Moon and Earth is very slowly increasing over time,[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Lambeck1977-199) the angular diameter of the Moon is decreasing. As it evolves toward becoming a [red giant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_giant "Red giant"), the size of the Sun, and its apparent diameter in the sky, are slowly increasing.[[l]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-size_changes-234) The combination of these two changes means that hundreds of millions of years ago, the Moon would always completely cover the Sun on solar eclipses, and no annular eclipses were possible. Likewise, hundreds of millions of years in the future, the Moon will no longer cover the Sun completely, and total solar eclipses will not occur.[[223]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-fourmilab-235)

As the Moon's orbit around Earth is inclined by about 5.145¬∞ (5¬∞ 9') to the [orbit of Earth around the Sun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecliptic "Ecliptic"), eclipses do not occur at every full and new moon. For an eclipse to occur, the Moon must be near the intersection of the two orbital planes.[[224]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-eclipse-236) The periodicity and recurrence of eclipses of the Sun by the Moon, and of the Moon by Earth, is described by the [saros](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saros_(astronomy) "Saros (astronomy)"), which has a period of approximately 18 years.[[225]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-237)

Because the Moon continuously blocks the view of a half-degree-wide circular area of the sky,[[m]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-area-238)[[226]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-239) the related phenomenon of [occultation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Occultation "Occultation") occurs when a bright star or planet passes behind the Moon and is occulted: hidden from view. In this way, a solar eclipse is an occultation of the Sun. Because the Moon is comparatively close to Earth, occultations of individual stars are not visible everywhere on the planet, nor at the same time. Because of the [precession](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Precession "Precession") of the lunar orbit, each year different stars are occulted.[[227]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-240)

### Moon illusion

The [Moon illusion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon_illusion "Moon illusion") is the [optical illusion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Optical_illusion "Optical illusion") of the Moon appearing larger near the [horizon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Horizon "Horizon") than it does higher up in the [sky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sky "Sky"). It has been known since ancient times and recorded by various cultures.[[228]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Moon_illusion_Wade-241)[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Moon_illusion_Ross_Plug-242) The explanation of this illusion is still debated.[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Moon_illusion_Ross_Plug-242)[[230]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Moon_illusion_Hershenson-243)[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-244)

History of exploration and human presence
-----------------------------------------

### Pre-telescopic observation (before 1609)

It is believed by some that the oldest [cave paintings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cave_painting "Cave painting") from up to 40,000 [BP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Before_present "Before present") of bulls and geometric shapes,[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-e093-245) or 20‚Äì30,000 year old [tally sticks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tally_stick "Tally stick") were used to observe the phases of the Moon, keeping time using the waxing and waning of [the Moon's phases](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_phases "Lunar phases").[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Burton2011-246) Aspects of the Moon were identified and aggregated in [lunar deities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_deities "Lunar deities") from [prehistoric times](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prehistoric_times "Prehistoric times") and were eventually documented and put into symbols from the very first instances of [writing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Writing "Writing") in the [4th millennium BC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/4th_millennium_BC "4th millennium BC"). One of the earliest-discovered possible depictions of the Moon is a 3,000 BCE rock carving _Orthostat 47_ at [Knowth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowth "Knowth"), Ireland.[[234]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Knowth-247)[[235]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-spacetoday-248) The [crescent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#Crescent) depicting the Moon as with the lunar deity [Nanna/Sin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sin_(mythology) "Sin (mythology)") have been found from the 3rd millennium BCE.[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-BlackGreen1992-249)

The oldest named astronomer and poet [Enheduanna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enheduanna "Enheduanna"), [Akkadian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Akkadian_Empire "Akkadian Empire") high priestess to the lunar deity Nanna/Sin and pricess, daughter of [Sargon the Great](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sargon_the_Great "Sargon the Great") (c. 2334 ‚Äì c. 2279 BCE), had the Moon tracked in her chambers.[[237]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-c099-250) The oldest found and identified depiction of the Moon in an astronomical relation to other astronomical features is the [Nebra sky disc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nebra_sky_disc "Nebra sky disc") from c. 1800‚Äì1600 BCE, depicting features like the [Pleiades](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pleiades "Pleiades") next to the Moon.[[238]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-g361-251)[[239]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-k874-252)

[![Image 35](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Nebra_solstice_2.jpg/250px-Nebra_solstice_2.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Nebra_solstice_2.jpg)

The [Nebra sky disc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nebra_sky_disc "Nebra sky disc") (c. 1800‚Äì1600 BCE), found near a possibly [astronomical complex](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astronomical_complex "Astronomical complex"), most likely depicting the Sun or full Moon, the Moon as a crescent, the [Pleiades](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pleiades "Pleiades") and the summer and winter solstices as strips of gold on the side of the disc,[[240]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Meller_2021-253)[[241]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-254) with the top representing the [horizon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Horizon "Horizon")[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-:03-255) and [north](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North "North").

The [ancient Greek](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greece "Ancient Greece") philosopher [Anaxagoras](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anaxagoras "Anaxagoras") (d. 428 BC) reasoned that the Sun and Moon were both giant spherical rocks, and that the latter reflected the light of the former.[[243]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-256)[[244]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Needham1986-257): 227  Elsewhere in the 5th century BC to 4th century BC, [Babylonian astronomers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Babylonian_astronomers "Babylonian astronomers") had recorded the 18-year [Saros cycle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saros_cycle "Saros cycle") of [lunar eclipses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_eclipse "Lunar eclipse"),[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-258) and [Indian astronomers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_astronomy "Indian astronomy") had described the Moon's monthly elongation.[[246]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Sarma-Ast-Ind-259) The [Chinese astronomer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_astronomer "Chinese astronomer")[Shi Shen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shi_Shen "Shi Shen")([fl.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fl. "Fl.") 4th century BC) gave instructions for predicting solar and lunar eclipses.[[244]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Needham1986-257): 411

In [Aristotle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aristotle "Aristotle")'s (384‚Äì322 BC) [description of the universe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/On_the_Heavens "On the Heavens"), the Moon marked the boundary between the spheres of the mutable elements (earth, water, air and fire), and the imperishable stars of [aether](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aether_(classical_element) "Aether (classical element)"), an [influential philosophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aristotelian_physics "Aristotelian physics") that would dominate for centuries.[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-260)[Archimedes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archimedes "Archimedes") (287‚Äì212 BC) designed a planetarium that could calculate the motions of the Moon and other objects in the Solar System.[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-261) In the 2nd century BC, [Seleucus of Seleucia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seleucus_of_Seleucia "Seleucus of Seleucia") correctly thought that [tides](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tide "Tide") were due to the attraction of the Moon, and that their height depends on the Moon's position relative to the [Sun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sun "Sun").[[249]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-262) In the same century, [Aristarchus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/On_the_Sizes_and_Distances_(Aristarchus) "On the Sizes and Distances (Aristarchus)") computed the size and distance of the Moon from Earth, obtaining a value of about twenty times the [radius of Earth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radius_of_Earth "Radius of Earth") for the distance.

The Chinese of the [Han dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Han_dynasty "Han dynasty") believed the Moon to be energy equated to _[qi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qi "Qi")_ and their 'radiating influence' theory recognized that the light of the Moon was merely a reflection of the Sun; [Jing Fang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jing_Fang "Jing Fang") (78‚Äì37 BC) noted the sphericity of the Moon.[[244]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Needham1986-257): 413‚Äì414 [Ptolemy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ptolemy "Ptolemy") (90‚Äì168 AD) greatly improved on the numbers of Aristarchus, calculating a mean distance of 59 times Earth's radius and a diameter of 0.292 Earth diameters, close to the correct values of about 60 and 0.273 respectively.[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-263) In the 2nd century AD, [Lucian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucian "Lucian") wrote the novel _[A True Story](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A\_True\_Story "A True Story")_, in which the heroes travel to the Moon and meet its inhabitants. In 510 AD, the Indian astronomer [Aryabhata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aryabhata "Aryabhata") mentioned in his _[Aryabhatiya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aryabhatiya "Aryabhatiya")_ that reflected sunlight is the cause of the shining of the Moon.[[251]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Hayashi08Aryabhata-264)[[252]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-265) The astronomer and physicist [Ibn al-Haytham](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ibn_al-Haytham "Ibn al-Haytham") (965‚Äì1039) found that [sunlight](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sunlight "Sunlight") was not reflected from the Moon like a mirror, but that light was emitted from every part of the Moon's sunlit surface in all directions.[[253]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-266)[Shen Kuo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shen_Kuo "Shen Kuo") (1031‚Äì1095) of the [Song dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Song_dynasty "Song dynasty") created an allegory equating the waxing and waning of the Moon to a round ball of reflective silver that, when doused with white powder and viewed from the side, would appear to be a crescent.[[244]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Needham1986-257): 415‚Äì416  During the [Middle Ages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Ages "Middle Ages"), before the invention of the telescope, the Moon was increasingly recognized as a sphere, though many believed that it was "perfectly smooth".[[254]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-267)

### Telescopic exploration (1609‚Äì1959)

[![Image 36](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Galileo%27s_sketches_of_the_moon_%28cropped%29.png/250px-Galileo%27s_sketches_of_the_moon_%28cropped%29.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Galileo%27s_sketches_of_the_moon_(cropped).png)

The first published sketches of one of the first telescopic observations of the Moon, from the ground-breaking _[Sidereus Nuncius](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sidereus\_Nuncius "Sidereus Nuncius")_ (1610) by [Galileo Galilei](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galileo_Galilei "Galileo Galilei"), providing among other findings the first descriptions of the Moon's topography

The [telescope](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Telescope "Telescope") was developed and reported on in 1608. The first record of telescopic astronomy and rough mapping of the Moon's features is from early summer 1609 by [Thomas Harriot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Harriot "Thomas Harriot"), but which he did not publish. At the same time [Galileo Galilei](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galileo_Galilei "Galileo Galilei") too started to use telescopes to observe the sky and the Moon, recording later that year more detailed observations and crucial conclusions, such as that the Moon was not smooth, featuring mountains and craters, which he published in 1610 in his ground-breaking and soon widely discussed book _[Sidereus Nuncius](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sidereus\_Nuncius "Sidereus Nuncius")_.

Later in the 17th century, the efforts of [Giovanni Battista Riccioli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giovanni_Battista_Riccioli "Giovanni Battista Riccioli") and [Francesco Maria Grimaldi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francesco_Maria_Grimaldi "Francesco Maria Grimaldi") led to the system of naming of lunar features in use today. The more exact 1834‚Äì1836 _[Mappa Selenographica](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mappa\_Selenographica "Mappa Selenographica")_ of [Wilhelm Beer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilhelm_Beer "Wilhelm Beer") and [Johann Heinrich von M√§dler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Heinrich_von_M%C3%A4dler "Johann Heinrich von M√§dler"), and their associated 1837 book _Der Mond_, the first [trigonometrically](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trigonometry "Trigonometry") accurate study of lunar features, included the heights of more than a thousand mountains, and introduced the study of the Moon at accuracies possible in earthly geography.[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-268) Lunar craters, first noted by Galileo, were thought to be [volcanic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volcanic "Volcanic") until the 1870s proposal of [Richard Proctor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Proctor "Richard Proctor") that they were formed by collisions.[[70]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-worldbook-78) This view gained support in 1892 from the experimentation of geologist [Grove Karl Gilbert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grove_Karl_Gilbert "Grove Karl Gilbert"), and from comparative studies from 1920 to the 1940s,[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Hall1977-269) leading to the development of [lunar stratigraphy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_geologic_timescale "Lunar geologic timescale"), which by the 1950s was becoming a new and growing branch of [astrogeology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astrogeology "Astrogeology").[[70]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-worldbook-78)

### First missions to the Moon (1959‚Äì1976)

After [World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II "World War II") the first [launch systems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Launch_system "Launch system") were developed and by the end of the 1950s they reached capabilities that allowed the [Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union") and the [United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States "United States") to launch [spacecraft](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spacecraft "Spacecraft") into space. The [Cold War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War "Cold War") fueled a closely followed development of launch systems by the two states, resulting in the so-called [Space Race](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_Race "Space Race") and its later phase the Moon Race, accelerating efforts and interest in [exploration of the Moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exploration_of_the_Moon "Exploration of the Moon").

[![Image 37](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Luna_3_moon.jpg/250px-Luna_3_moon.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Luna_3_moon.jpg)

First view of the [far side of the Moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Far_side_of_the_Moon "Far side of the Moon"), taken by [Luna 3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luna_3 "Luna 3"), October 7, 1959. Clearly visible is [Mare Moscoviense](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mare_Moscoviense "Mare Moscoviense") (top right) and a mare triplet of [Mare Crisium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mare_Crisium "Mare Crisium"), [Mare Marginis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mare_Marginis "Mare Marginis") and [Mare Smythii](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mare_Smythii "Mare Smythii") (left center).

After the first spaceflight of [Sputnik 1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sputnik_1 "Sputnik 1") in 1957 during [International Geophysical Year](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Geophysical_Year "International Geophysical Year") the spacecraft of the Soviet Union's [_Luna_ program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luna_programme "Luna programme") were the first to accomplish a number of goals. Following three unnamed failed missions in 1958,[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-270) the first human-made object _[Luna 1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luna\_1 "Luna 1")_ escaped Earth's gravity and passed near the Moon in 1959. Later that year the first human-made object _[Luna 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luna\_2 "Luna 2")_ reached the Moon's surface by [intentionally impacting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lander_(spacecraft)#Impactors "Lander (spacecraft)"). By the end of the year _[Luna 3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luna\_3 "Luna 3")_ reached as the first human-made object the normally occluded [far side of the Moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Far_side_of_the_Moon "Far side of the Moon"), taking the first photographs of it. The first spacecraft to perform a successful lunar [soft landing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lander_(spacecraft) "Lander (spacecraft)") was _[Luna 9](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luna\_9 "Luna 9")_ and the first vehicle to orbit the Moon was _[Luna 10](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luna\_10 "Luna 10")_, both in 1966.[[70]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-worldbook-78)

[![Image 38: The small blue-white semicircle of Earth, almost glowing with color in the blackness of space, rising over the limb of the desolate, cratered surface of the Moon.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/NASA-Apollo8-Dec24-Earthrise.jpg/250px-NASA-Apollo8-Dec24-Earthrise.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:NASA-Apollo8-Dec24-Earthrise.jpg)

_[Earthrise](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earthrise "Earthrise")_, the first color [image of Earth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_first_images_of_Earth_from_space "Timeline of first images of Earth from space") taken by a human from the Moon, during [Apollo 8](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_8 "Apollo 8") (1968), the first time a crewed spacecraft left Earth orbit and reached another [astronomical body](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astronomical_body "Astronomical body")

Following President [John F. Kennedy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_F._Kennedy "John F. Kennedy")'s 1961 commitment to a crewed Moon landing before the end of the decade, the United States, under NASA leadership, launched a series of uncrewed probes to develop an understanding of the lunar surface in preparation for human missions: the [Jet Propulsion Laboratory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory "Jet Propulsion Laboratory")'s [Ranger program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ranger_program "Ranger program"), the [Lunar Orbiter program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_Orbiter_program "Lunar Orbiter program") and the [Surveyor program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surveyor_program "Surveyor program"). The crewed [Apollo program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_program "Apollo program") was developed in parallel; after a series of uncrewed and crewed tests of the Apollo spacecraft in Earth orbit, and spurred on by a potential [Soviet lunar human landing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_human_lunar_programs "Soviet human lunar programs"), in 1968 [Apollo 8](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_8 "Apollo 8") made the first human mission to lunar orbit (the first Earthlings, two tortoises, had circled the Moon three months earlier on the Soviet Union's [Zond 5](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zond_5 "Zond 5"), followed by turtles on [Zond 6](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zond_6 "Zond 6")).

The first time a person landed on the Moon and any extraterrestrial body was when [Neil Armstrong](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neil_Armstrong "Neil Armstrong"), the commander of the American mission [Apollo 11](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_11 "Apollo 11"), set foot on the Moon at 02:56 UTC on July 21, 1969.[[258]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-271) Considered the culmination of the [Space Race](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_Race "Space Race"),[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-CNN-272) an estimated 500 million people worldwide watched the transmission by the [Apollo TV camera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_TV_camera "Apollo TV camera"), the largest television audience for a live broadcast at that time.[[260]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-273)[[261]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-274) While at the same time another mission, the robotic sample return mission [Luna 15](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luna_15 "Luna 15") by the Soviet Union had been in orbit around the Moon, becoming together with Apollo 11 the first ever case of two extraterrestrial missions being conducted at the same time.

The Apollo missions 11 to 17 (except [Apollo 13](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_13 "Apollo 13"), which aborted its planned lunar landing) removed 380.05 kilograms (837.87 lb) of lunar rock and soil in 2,196 [separate samples](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon_rock "Moon rock").[[262]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-275) Scientific instrument packages were installed on the lunar surface during all the Apollo landings. Long-lived [instrument stations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_Lunar_Surface_Experiments_Package "Apollo Lunar Surface Experiments Package"), including heat flow probes, [seismometers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seismometer "Seismometer"), and [magnetometers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magnetometer "Magnetometer"), were installed at the [Apollo 12](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_12 "Apollo 12"), [14](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_14 "Apollo 14"), [15](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_15 "Apollo 15"), [16](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_16 "Apollo 16"), and [17](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_17 "Apollo 17") landing sites. Direct transmission of data to Earth concluded in late 1977 because of budgetary considerations,[[263]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-276)[[264]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-277) but as the stations' [lunar laser ranging](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_laser_ranging "Lunar laser ranging") corner-cube retroreflector arrays are passive instruments, they are still being used.[[265]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-278)[Apollo 17](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_17 "Apollo 17") in 1972 remains the last crewed mission to the Moon. [Explorer 49](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Explorer_49 "Explorer 49") in 1973 was the last dedicated U.S. probe to the Moon until the 1994.

[![Image 39](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/AS12-48-7133_%2821470506269%29.jpg/250px-AS12-48-7133_%2821470506269%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:AS12-48-7133_(21470506269).jpg)

An example of the robotic and human exploration of the Moon in a first ever [visit of a separate mission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_rendezvous "Space rendezvous") beyond [Low Earth Orbit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Low_Earth_Orbit "Low Earth Orbit")[[266]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-g936-279), [Apollo 12](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_12 "Apollo 12") astronaut [Pete Conrad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pete_Conrad "Pete Conrad") checking on [Surveyor 3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surveyor_3 "Surveyor 3") at their shared [lunar base](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_base "Lunar base"), with the Apollo 12 _Intrepid_ lander and S-band antenna in the distant background

The Soviet Union continued sending robotic missions to the Moon until 1976, deploying in 1970 with [Luna 17](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luna_17 "Luna 17") the first remote controlled [rover](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rover_(space_exploration) "Rover (space exploration)")[Lunokhod 1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunokhod_1 "Lunokhod 1") on an extraterrestrial surface, and collecting and returning 0.3 kg of rock and soil samples with three _Luna_[sample return missions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sample_return_mission "Sample return mission") (_[Luna 16](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luna\_16 "Luna 16")_ in 1970, _[Luna 20](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luna\_20 "Luna 20")_ in 1972, and _[Luna 24](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luna\_24 "Luna 24")_ in 1976).[[267]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-280)

### Moon Treaty and explorational absence (1976‚Äì1990)

Following the [last Soviet mission to the Moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luna_24 "Luna 24") of 1976, there was little further lunar exploration for fourteen years. Astronautics had shifted its focus towards the exploration of the [inner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inner_Solar_System "Inner Solar System") (e.g. [Venera program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venera_program "Venera program")) and [outer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Outer_Solar_System "Outer Solar System") (e.g. [Pioneer 10](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pioneer_10 "Pioneer 10"), 1972) [Solar System](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System "Solar System")[planets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planet "Planet"), but also towards [Earth orbit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geocentric_orbit "Geocentric orbit"), developing and continuously operating, beside [communication satellites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communication_satellite "Communication satellite"), [Earth observation satellites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth_observation_satellite "Earth observation satellite") (e.g. [Landsat program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Landsat_program "Landsat program"), 1972), [space telescopes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_telescope "Space telescope") and particularly [space stations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_station "Space station") (e.g. [Salyut program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salyut_program "Salyut program"), 1971).

Negotiation in 1979 of [Moon treaty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon_treaty "Moon treaty"), and its subsequent ratification in 1984 was the only major activity regarding the Moon until 1990.

### Renewed exploration (1990‚Äìpresent)

In 1990 _[Hiten](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hiten\_(spacecraft) "Hiten (spacecraft)")_ ‚Äì _Hagoromo_,[[268]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-281) the first dedicated lunar mission since 1976, reached the Moon. Sent by [Japan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japan "Japan"), it became the first mission that was not a Soviet Union or U.S. mission to the Moon.

In 1994, the U.S. dedicated a mission to fly a spacecraft (_[Clementine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clementine\_(spacecraft) "Clementine (spacecraft)")_) to the Moon again for the first time since 1973. This mission obtained the first near-global topographic map of the Moon, and the first global [multispectral](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multispectral "Multispectral") images of the lunar surface.[[269]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-282) In 1998, this was followed by the _[Lunar Prospector](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar\_Prospector "Lunar Prospector")_ mission, whose instruments indicated the presence of excess hydrogen at the lunar poles, which is likely to have been caused by the presence of water ice in the upper few meters of the regolith within permanently shadowed craters.[[270]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-283)

The next years saw a row of first missions to the Moon by a new group of states actively exploring the Moon. Between 2004 and 2006 the first spacecraft by the [European Space Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Space_Agency "European Space Agency") (ESA) (_[SMART-1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SMART-1 "SMART-1")_) reached the Moon, recording the first detailed survey of chemical elements on the lunar surface.[[271]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-284) The [Chinese Lunar Exploration Program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_Lunar_Exploration_Program "Chinese Lunar Exploration Program") reached the Moon for the first time with the orbiter _[Chang'e 1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chang%27e\_1 "Chang'e 1")_ (2007‚Äì2009),[[272]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-285) obtaining a full image map of the Moon. [India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Space_Research_Organisation "Indian Space Research Organisation") reached, orbited and impacted the Moon in 2008 for the first time with its _[Chandrayaan-1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chandrayaan-1 "Chandrayaan-1")_ and [Moon Impact Probe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon_Impact_Probe "Moon Impact Probe"), becoming the fifth and sixth state to do so, creating a high-resolution chemical, mineralogical and photo-geological map of the lunar surface, and confirming the presence of [water molecules in lunar soil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_water "Lunar water").[[273]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-286)

The U.S. launched the [_Lunar Reconnaissance Orbiter_ (LRO)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_Reconnaissance_Orbiter "Lunar Reconnaissance Orbiter") and the _[LCROSS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LCROSS "LCROSS")_ impactor on June 18, 2009. _LCROSS_ completed its mission by making a planned and widely observed impact in the crater [Cabeus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cabeus "Cabeus") on October 9, 2009,[[274]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-287) whereas _LRO_ is currently in operation, obtaining precise lunar [altimetry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Altimetry "Altimetry") and high-resolution imagery.

China continued its lunar program in 2010 with _[Chang'e 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chang%27e\_2 "Chang'e 2")_, mapping the surface at a higher resolution over an eight-month period, and in 2013 with _[Chang'e 3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chang%27e\_3 "Chang'e 3")_, a lunar [lander](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lander_(spacecraft) "Lander (spacecraft)") along with a [lunar rover](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_rover "Lunar rover") named _[Yutu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yutu\_(rover) "Yutu (rover)")_ ([Chinese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_language "Chinese language"): ÁéâÂÖî; lit. 'Jade Rabbit'). This was the first lunar rover mission since _[Lunokhod 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunokhod\_2 "Lunokhod 2")_ in 1973 and the first lunar [soft landing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soft_landing "Soft landing") since _[Luna 24](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luna\_24 "Luna 24")_ in 1976, making China the third country to achieve this.

In 2014 the first privately funded probe, the [Manfred Memorial Moon Mission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manfred_Memorial_Moon_Mission "Manfred Memorial Moon Mission"), reached the Moon.

Another Chinese rover mission, _[Chang'e 4](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chang%27e\_4 "Chang'e 4")_, achieved the first landing on [the Moon's far side](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Far_side_of_the_Moon "Far side of the Moon") in early 2019.[[275]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-288)

Also in 2019, India successfully sent its second probe, _[Chandrayaan-2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chandrayaan-2 "Chandrayaan-2")_ to the Moon.

In 2020, China carried out its first robotic [sample return mission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sample_return_mission "Sample return mission") (_[Chang'e 5](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chang%27e\_5 "Chang'e 5")_), bringing back 1,731 grams of lunar material to Earth.[[276]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-289)

The U.S. [developed plans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vision_for_Space_Exploration "Vision for Space Exploration") for returning to the Moon beginning in 2004,[[277]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-290) and with the signing of the U.S.-led [Artemis Accords](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_Accords "Artemis Accords") in 2020, the [Artemis program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program "Artemis program") aims to return the astronauts to the Moon in the 2020s.[[278]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-291) The Accords have been joined by a growing number of countries. The introduction of the Artemis Accords has fueled a renewed discussion about the international framework and cooperation of lunar activity, building on the [Moon Treaty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon_Treaty "Moon Treaty") and the ESA-led [Moon Village](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon_Village "Moon Village") concept.[[279]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-The_Space_Review_2020-292)[[280]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Australian_Institute_of_International_Affairs_2021-293)[[281]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-The_Space_Treaty_Institute_%E2%80%93_Dedicated_to_Peace_and_Sustainability_in_Outer_Space._Our_Mission-294)

2022 [South Korea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Korea "South Korea") launched [Danuri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Danuri "Danuri") successfully, its first mission to the Moon, launched from the US. 2023 and 2024 [India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India "India") and Japan became the fourth and fifth country to [soft land](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soft_landing "Soft landing") a spacecraft on the Moon, following the [Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union") and [United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States "United States") in the 1960s, and [China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China "China") in the 2010s.[[282]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-295) Notably, Japan's spacecraft, the [Smart Lander for Investigating Moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Smart_Lander_for_Investigating_Moon "Smart Lander for Investigating Moon"), survived 3 lunar nights.[[283]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-296) The [IM-1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IM-1 "IM-1") lander became the first commercially built lander to land on the Moon in 2024.[[284]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-297)

China launched the [Chang'e 6](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chang%27e_6 "Chang'e 6") on May 3, 2024, which conducted another lunar sample return from the [far side of the Moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Far_side_of_the_Moon "Far side of the Moon").[[285]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-AJ_FI-20230425-298) It also carried a Chinese rover to conduct [infrared spectroscopy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Absorption_spectroscopy "Absorption spectroscopy") of lunar surface.[[286]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-299)[Pakistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan "Pakistan") sent a lunar orbiter called [ICUBE-Q](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ICUBE-Q "ICUBE-Q") along with Chang'e 6.[[287]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-300)

[Nova-C 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IM-2 "IM-2"), [iSpace Lander](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ispace_(Japanese_company)#Hakuto-R_program "Ispace (Japanese company)") and [Blue Ghost](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blue_Ghost "Blue Ghost") were all launched to the Moon in 2024.

[![Image 40](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Artemis_2_Crew_Portrait.jpg/250px-Artemis_2_Crew_Portrait.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Artemis_2_Crew_Portrait.jpg)

[Artemis II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_II "Artemis II") crew, with the [first woman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_space "Women in space"), person of color and non‚ÄìUS-citizen astronaut planned to go to the Moon, scheduled for 2026, returning humans to the Moon for the first time since [Apollo 17](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_17 "Apollo 17") in 1972. [Clockwise](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clockwise "Clockwise") from left: [Koch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christina_Koch "Christina Koch"), [Glover](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Victor_J._Glover "Victor J. Glover"), [Hansen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeremy_Hansen "Jeremy Hansen") and [Wiseman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reid_Wiseman "Reid Wiseman").

### Future

Beside the progressing [Artemis program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program "Artemis program") and supporting [Commercial Lunar Payload Services](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commercial_Lunar_Payload_Services "Commercial Lunar Payload Services"), leading an international and commercial crewed opening up of the Moon and sending the [first woman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_space "Women in space"), person of color and non-US citizen to the Moon in the 2020s,[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-301) China is continuing its ambitious [Chang'e program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chang%27e_program "Chang'e program"), having announced with Russia's struggling _[Luna-Glob](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luna-Glob "Luna-Glob")_ program joint missions.[[289]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-TASS_2019_x202-302)[[290]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-303) Both the Chinese and US lunar programs have the goal to establish in the 2030s a [lunar base](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_base "Lunar base") with their international partners, though the US and its partners will first establish an orbital [Lunar Gateway](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_Gateway "Lunar Gateway") station in the 2020s, from which Artemis missions will land the [Human Landing System](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_Landing_System "Human Landing System") to set up temporary surface camps.

While the Apollo missions were explorational in nature, the Artemis program plans to establish a more permanent presence. To this end, NASA is partnering with industry leaders to establish key elements such as modern communication infrastructure. A [4G](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/4G "4G") connectivity demonstration is to be launched aboard an [Intuitive Machines Nova-C](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intuitive_Machines_Nova-C "Intuitive Machines Nova-C") lander in 2024.[[291]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-304) Another focus is on [in situ resource utilization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/In_situ_resource_utilization "In situ resource utilization"), which is a key part of the [DARPA lunar programs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DARPA_lunar_programs "DARPA lunar programs"). [DARPA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DARPA "DARPA") has requested that industry partners develop a 10‚Äìyear lunar architecture plan to enable the beginning of a lunar economy.[[292]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-305)

Human presence
--------------

[![Image 41](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Moon_Soft_Landings.svg/250px-Moon_Soft_Landings.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Moon_Soft_Landings.svg)

Map of all the sites of [soft landings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soft_landing "Soft landing") on the Moon (2024)

In 1959 the first extraterrestrial probes reached the Moon ([Luna program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luna_program "Luna program")), just a year into the [space age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_age "Space age"), after the first ever orbital flight. Since then, humans have sent a range of probes and people to the Moon. The first stay of people on the Moon was conducted in 1969, in a series of crewed exploration missions (the [Apollo Program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_Program "Apollo Program")), the last having taken place in 1972.

Uninterrupted presence has been the case through the [remains](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_artificial_objects_on_the_Moon "List of artificial objects on the Moon") of impactors, landings and [lunar orbiters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_extraterrestrial_orbiters#Moon "List of extraterrestrial orbiters"). Some landings and orbiters have maintained a small lunar infrastructure, providing continuous observation and communication at the Moon.

Increasing human activity in [cislunar space](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cislunar_space "Cislunar space") as well as on the Moon's surface, particularly missions at the far side of the Moon or the [lunar north](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_north_pole "Lunar north pole") and [south polar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_south_pole "Lunar south pole") regions, are in need for a lunar infrastructure. For that purpose, orbiters in [orbits around the Moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_orbit "Lunar orbit") or [the Earth‚ÄìMoon Lagrange points](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_objects_at_Lagrange_points#Earth%E2%80%93Moon_Lagrange_points "List of objects at Lagrange points"), have since 2006 been operated. With highly [eccentric orbits](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orbital_eccentricity "Orbital eccentricity") providing continuous communication, as with the orbit of [Queqiao](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Queqiao "Queqiao") and [Queqiao-2 relay satellite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Queqiao-2_relay_satellite "Queqiao-2 relay satellite") or the planned first extraterrestrial space station, the [Lunar Gateway](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_Gateway "Lunar Gateway").[[293]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Williams_2022-306)[[294]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Phys.org_2021-307)

### Human impact

[![Image 42](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/ALSEP_AS17-134-20500.jpg/250px-ALSEP_AS17-134-20500.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:ALSEP_AS17-134-20500.jpg)

Artifacts of human activity, [Apollo 17's Lunar Surface Experiments Package](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_Lunar_Surface_Experiments_Package "Apollo Lunar Surface Experiments Package")[[295]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Garber_2012-308)

While the Moon has the lowest [planetary protection target-categorization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_protection#Target_categories "Planetary protection"), its degradation as a pristine body and scientific place has been discussed.[[296]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Vidaurri_2019-309) If there is [astronomy performed from the Moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#Astronomy_from_the_Moon), it will need to be free from any physical and [radio pollution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radio_pollution "Radio pollution"). While the Moon has no significant atmosphere, traffic and impacts on the Moon causes clouds of dust that can spread far and possibly contaminate the original state of the Moon and its special scientific content.[[297]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-David_2020-310) Scholar [Alice Gorman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alice_Gorman "Alice Gorman") asserts that, although the Moon is inhospitable, it is not dead, and that sustainable human activity would require treating the Moon's ecology as a co-participant.[[298]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Gorman_2022-311)

The so-called "[Tardigrade affair](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tardigrades_on_the_Moon "Tardigrades on the Moon")" of the 2019 crashed [Beresheet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beresheet "Beresheet") lander and its carrying of [tardigrades](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tardigrade "Tardigrade") has been discussed as an example for lacking measures and lacking international regulation for [planetary protection](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_protection "Planetary protection").[[299]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Alvarez_2020_p.-312)

[Space debris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_debris "Space debris") beyond Earth around the Moon has been considered as a future challenge with increasing numbers of missions to the Moon, particularly as a danger for such missions.[[300]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Carter_2022-313)[[301]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Nast_2013-314) As such lunar waste management has been raised as an issue which future lunar missions, particularly on the surface, need to tackle.[[302]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Pino_Salmeri_Hugo_Hume_p.-315)[[303]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-NASA/ADS-316)

Human remains have been transported to the Moon, including by private companies such as [Celestis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celestis "Celestis") and [Elysium Space](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elysium_Space "Elysium Space"). Because the Moon has been sacred or significant to many cultures, the practice of [space burials](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_burial "Space burial") have attracted criticism from [indigenous peoples](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indigenous_peoples "Indigenous peoples") leaders. For example, then‚Äì[Navajo Nation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Navajo_Nation "Navajo Nation") president [Albert Hale](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Hale "Albert Hale") criticized NASA for sending the [cremated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cremated "Cremated") ashes of scientist [Eugene Shoemaker](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eugene_Shoemaker "Eugene Shoemaker") to the Moon in 1998.[[304]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Magazine_Sullivan_2024_a329-317)[[305]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-web.archive.org_2011_c901-318)

Beside the remains of human activity on the Moon, there have been some intended permanent installations like the _[Moon Museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon\_Museum "Moon Museum")_ art piece, [Apollo 11 goodwill messages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_11_goodwill_messages "Apollo 11 goodwill messages"), six [lunar plaques](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_plaque "Lunar plaque"), the _[Fallen Astronaut](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fallen\_Astronaut "Fallen Astronaut")_ memorial, and other artifacts.[[295]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Garber_2012-308)
