Longterm missions continuing to be active are some orbiters such as the 2009-launched [Lunar Reconnaissance Orbiter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_Reconnaissance_Orbiter "Lunar Reconnaissance Orbiter") surveilling the Moon for future missions, as well as some Landers such as the 2013-launched [Chang'e 3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chang%27e_3 "Chang'e 3") with its Lunar Ultraviolet Telescope still operational.[[306]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-319) Five retroreflectors have been installed on the Moon since the 1970s and since used for accurate measurements of the physical [librations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Libration "Libration") through [laser ranging to the Moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_Laser_Ranging_experiment "Lunar Laser Ranging experiment").

There are [several missions by different agencies and companies planned](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_missions_to_the_Moon#Future_missions "List of missions to the Moon") to establish a long-term human presence on the Moon, with the [Lunar Gateway](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_Gateway "Lunar Gateway") as the currently most advanced project as part of the [Artemis program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program "Artemis program").

### Astronomy from the Moon

[![Image 43](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Earth%E2%80%99s_geocorona_from_the_Moon.jpg/250px-Earth%E2%80%99s_geocorona_from_the_Moon.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Earth%E2%80%99s_geocorona_from_the_Moon.jpg)

Earth's [exosphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exosphere "Exosphere") illuminated creating its [geocorona](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geocorona "Geocorona"), visible in ultraviolet and viewed by the [Far Ultraviolet Camera/Spectrograph](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Far_Ultraviolet_Camera/Spectrograph "Far Ultraviolet Camera/Spectrograph") of [Apollo 16](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_16 "Apollo 16") in 1972 from the Moon's surface

The Moon has been used as a site for astronomical and [Earth observations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth_observation "Earth observation"). The Earth appears in the [Moon's sky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extraterrestrial_sky#The_Moon "Extraterrestrial sky") with an [apparent size](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apparent_size "Apparent size") of 1¬∞ 48‚Ä≤ to 2¬∞,[[307]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Gorkavyi_Krotkov_Marshak_2023_pp._1527%E2%80%931537-320) three to four times the size of the Moon or Sun in Earth's sky, or about the apparent width of two little fingers at an arm's length away. Observations from the Moon started as early as 1966 with the [first images of Earth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_first_images_of_Earth_from_space "Timeline of first images of Earth from space") from the Moon, taken by [Lunar Orbiter 1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_Orbiter_1 "Lunar Orbiter 1"). Of particular cultural significance is the 1968 photograph called _[Earthrise](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earthrise "Earthrise")_, taken by [Bill Anders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Anders "Bill Anders") of [Apollo 8](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_8 "Apollo 8") in 1968. In April 1972 the [Apollo 16](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_16 "Apollo 16") mission set up the first dedicated telescope,[[308]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-w422-321)[[309]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-x909-322) the [Far Ultraviolet Camera/Spectrograph](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Far_Ultraviolet_Camera/Spectrograph "Far Ultraviolet Camera/Spectrograph"), recording various astronomical photos and spectra.[[310]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-323)

The Moon is recognized as an excellent site for telescopes.[[311]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-324) It is relatively nearby; certain craters near the poles are permanently dark and cold and especially useful for [infrared telescopes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infrared_telescope "Infrared telescope"); and [radio telescopes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radio_telescope "Radio telescope") on the far side would be shielded from the radio chatter of Earth.[[312]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-325) The [lunar soil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_soil "Lunar soil"), although it poses a problem for any moving parts of [telescopes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Telescope "Telescope"), can be mixed with [carbon nanotubes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_nanotube "Carbon nanotube") and [epoxies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epoxy "Epoxy") and employed in the construction of mirrors up to 50 meters in diameter.[[313]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-326) A lunar [zenith telescope](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zenith_telescope "Zenith telescope") can be made cheaply with an [ionic liquid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ionic_liquid "Ionic liquid").[[314]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-327)

### Living on the Moon

[![Image 44](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Aldrin_Looks_Back_at_Tranquility_Base_-_GPN-2000-001102.jpg/250px-Aldrin_Looks_Back_at_Tranquility_Base_-_GPN-2000-001102.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Aldrin_Looks_Back_at_Tranquility_Base_-_GPN-2000-001102.jpg)

Astronaut [Buzz Aldrin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buzz_Aldrin "Buzz Aldrin") in [life-supporting suit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo/Skylab_spacesuit "Apollo/Skylab spacesuit") looking back at the first [lunar habitat and base](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_base "Lunar base"), the [Lunar Module _Eagle_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_Module_Eagle "Lunar Module Eagle") of [Tranquility Base](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tranquility_Base "Tranquility Base"), during [Apollo 11](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_11 "Apollo 11") (1969), the first crewed [Moon landing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon_landing "Moon landing")

The only instances of [humans living on the Moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_habitat_(facility)#Extraterrestrial_surface_habitat "Space habitat (facility)") have taken place in an [Apollo Lunar Module](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_Lunar_Module "Apollo Lunar Module") for several days at a time (for example, during the [Apollo 17](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_17 "Apollo 17") mission).[[315]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-328) One challenge to astronauts during their stay on the surface is that [lunar dust](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_dust "Lunar dust") sticks to their suits and is carried into their quarters. Astronauts could taste and smell the dust, which smells like gunpowder and was called the "Apollo aroma".[[316]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Aroma-329) This fine lunar dust can [cause health issues](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_dust#Harmful_effects_of_lunar_dust "Lunar dust").[[316]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Aroma-329)

In 2019, at least one plant seed sprouted in an experiment on the [Chang'e 4 lander](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Change_4#Lunar_lander "Change 4"). It was carried from Earth along with other small life in its _Lunar Micro Ecosystem_.[[317]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Seeds-330)

Legal status
------------

Although _[Luna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luna\_program "Luna program")_ landers scattered pennants of the [Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union") on the Moon, and [U.S. flags](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_Flag_Assembly "Lunar Flag Assembly") were symbolically planted at their landing sites by the [Apollo astronauts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_astronauts "Apollo astronauts"), no nation claims ownership of any part of the Moon's surface.[[318]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-unoosa_q6-331) Likewise no [private ownership of parts of the Moon, or as a whole](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extraterrestrial_real_estate "Extraterrestrial real estate"), is considered credible.[[319]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-unoosa_q7-332)[[320]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-iisl_2004-333)[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-iisl_2009-334)

The 1967 [Outer Space Treaty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Outer_Space_Treaty "Outer Space Treaty") defines the Moon and all outer space as the "[province of all mankind](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Common_heritage_of_mankind "Common heritage of mankind")".[[318]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-unoosa_q6-331) It restricts the use of the Moon to peaceful purposes, explicitly banning military installations and [weapons of mass destruction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weapons_of_mass_destruction "Weapons of mass destruction").[[322]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-unoosa_q5-335) A majority of countries are parties of this treaty.[[323]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-unoosa_q4-336) The 1979 [Moon Agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon_Agreement "Moon Agreement") was created to elaborate, and restrict the exploitation of the [Moon's resources](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_resources "Lunar resources") by any single nation, leaving it to a yet unspecified international regulatory regime.[[324]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-The_Space_Review_2021-337) As of January 2020, it has been signed and ratified by 18 nations,[[325]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-unoosa_moon-338) none of which have [human spaceflight](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_spaceflight "Human spaceflight") capabilities.

Since 2020, countries have joined the U.S. in their [Artemis Accords](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_Accords "Artemis Accords"), which are challenging the treaty. The U.S. has furthermore emphasized in a presidential [executive order](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executive_order "Executive order") ("Encouraging International Support for the Recovery and Use of Space Resources.") that "the United States does not view outer space as a 'global commons'" and calls the Moon Agreement "a failed attempt at constraining free enterprise."[[326]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-339)[[327]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-340)

With Australia signing and ratifying both the Moon Treaty in 1986 as well as the Artemis Accords in 2020, there has been a discussion if they can be harmonized.[[280]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Australian_Institute_of_International_Affairs_2021-293) In this light an _Implementation Agreement_ for the Moon Treaty has been advocated for, as a way to compensate for the shortcomings of the Moon Treaty and to harmonize it with other laws and agreements such as the Artemis Accords, allowing it to be more widely accepted.[[279]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-The_Space_Review_2020-292)[[281]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-The_Space_Treaty_Institute_%E2%80%93_Dedicated_to_Peace_and_Sustainability_in_Outer_Space._Our_Mission-294)

In the face of such increasing commercial and national interest, particularly prospecting territories, U.S. lawmakers have introduced in late 2020 specific regulation for the conservation of historic landing sites[[328]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-HowStuffWorks_2021-341) and interest groups have argued for making such sites [World Heritage Sites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Heritage_Site "World Heritage Site")[[329]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-For_All_Moonkind-342) and zones of scientific value protected zones, all of which add to the legal availability and territorialization of the Moon.[[299]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Alvarez_2020_p.-312)

In 2021, the _Declaration of the Rights of the Moon_[[330]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Declaration-343) was created by a group of "lawyers, space archaeologists and concerned citizens", drawing on precedents in the [Rights of Nature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rights_of_Nature "Rights of Nature") movement and the concept of legal personality for non-human entities in space.[[331]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-344)[[332]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Evans_2021-345)

### Coordination and regulation

Increasing human activity at the Moon has raised the need for coordination to safeguard international and commercial lunar activity. Issues from cooperation to mere coordination, through for example the development of a shared [Lunar time](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_time "Lunar time"), have been raised.

In particular the establishment of an [international](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internationalism_(politics) "Internationalism (politics)") or [United Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations") regulatory regime for lunar human activity has been called for by the [Moon Treaty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon_Treaty "Moon Treaty") and suggested through an _Implementation Agreement_,[[279]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-The_Space_Review_2020-292)[[281]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-The_Space_Treaty_Institute_%E2%80%93_Dedicated_to_Peace_and_Sustainability_in_Outer_Space._Our_Mission-294) but remains contentious. Current lunar programs are [multilateral](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multilateralism "Multilateralism"), with the US-led [Artemis program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program "Artemis program") and the China-led [International Lunar Research Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Lunar_Research_Station "International Lunar Research Station"). For broader international cooperation and coordination, the [International Lunar Exploration Working Group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Lunar_Exploration_Working_Group "International Lunar Exploration Working Group") (ILEWG), the [Moon Village Association](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon_Village "Moon Village") (MVA) and more generally the International Space Exploration Coordination Group (ISECG) has been established.

In culture and life
-------------------

### Timekeeping

[![Image 45](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Venus-de-Laussel-detail-corne.jpg/250px-Venus-de-Laussel-detail-corne.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Venus-de-Laussel-detail-corne.jpg)

The [Venus of Laussel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus_of_Laussel "Venus of Laussel") (c. 25,000 [BP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Before_present "Before present")) holding a crescent shaped horn. The 13 notches on the horn may symbolize the average number of days from menstruation to an [ovulation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ovulation "Ovulation"), or the approximate number of full [menstrual cycles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Menstrual_cycle "Menstrual cycle") and [lunar cycles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_cycle "Lunar cycle") per year (although these two phenomena are unrelated).[[333]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-:0b-346)[[334]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Boyle_2019-347)

Since pre-historic times people have taken note of [the Moon's phases](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_phases "Lunar phases") and its [waxing and waning cycle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_cycle "Lunar cycle") and used it to keep record of time. [Tally sticks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tally_stick "Tally stick"), notched bones dating as far back as 20‚Äì30,000 years ago, are believed by some to mark the phases of the Moon.[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Burton2011-246)[[335]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-348)[[336]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-349) The counting of the days between the Moon's phases eventually gave rise to generalized [time periods](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unit_of_time "Unit of time") of lunar cycles as [months](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Month "Month"), and possibly of its phases as [weeks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Week "Week").[[337]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Zerubavel_1989_p._9-350)

The words for the month in a range of different languages carry this relation between the period of the month and the Moon etymologically. The English _month_ as well as _moon_, and its cognates in other Indo-European languages (e.g. the [Latin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin "Latin")_mensis_ and [Ancient Greek](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greek "Ancient Greek")ŒºŒµŒØœÇ (_meis_) or ŒºŒÆŒΩ (mƒìn), meaning "month")[[338]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-351)[[339]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-352)[[340]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-353)[[341]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-354) stem from the [Proto-Indo-European](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-European "Proto-Indo-European") (PIE) root of _moon_, *_m√©h 1 n≈çt_, derived from the PIE verbal root *_meh 1_-, "to measure", "indicat[ing] a functional conception of the Moon, i.e. marker of the month" ([cf.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cf. "Cf.") the English words _measure_ and _menstrual_).[[342]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-355)[[343]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-356)[[344]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-357) To give another example from a different [language family](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Language_family "Language family"), the [Chinese language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_language "Chinese language") uses the same word ([Êúà](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%9C%88 "wikt:Êúà")) for _moon_ as for _month_, which furthermore can be found in the symbols for the word _week_ ([ÊòüÊúü](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%98%9F%E6%9C%9F "wikt:ÊòüÊúü")).

This lunar timekeeping gave rise to the historically dominant, but varied, [lunisolar calendars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunisolar_calendar "Lunisolar calendar"). The 7th-century [Islamic calendar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_calendar "Islamic calendar") is an example of a purely [lunar calendar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_calendar "Lunar calendar"), where months are traditionally determined by the visual sighting of the hilal, or earliest crescent moon, over the horizon.[[345]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-358)

Of particular significance has been the occasion of [full moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Full_moon "Full moon"), highlighted and celebrated in a range of calendars and cultures, an example being the Buddhist [Vesak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vesak "Vesak"). The full moon around the [southern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/March_equinox "March equinox") or [northern autumnal equinox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/September_equinox "September equinox") is often called the [harvest moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harvest_moon "Harvest moon") and is celebrated with festivities such as the [Harvest Moon Festival](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harvest_Moon_Festival "Harvest Moon Festival") of the [Chinese lunar calendar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_lunar_calendar "Chinese lunar calendar"), its second most important celebration after [the Chinese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_New_Year "Chinese New Year") lunisolar [Lunar New Year](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_New_Year "Lunar New Year").[[346]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Confucius_Institute_for_Scotland_2022-359)

Furthermore, association of time with the Moon can also be found in religion, such as the ancient Egyptian temporal and lunar deity [Khonsu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khonsu "Khonsu").

### Cultural representation

[![Image 46: Sumerian cylinder seal and impression, dated c. 2100 BC, of ·∏™a≈°·∏´amer, ensi (governor) of I≈°kun-Sin c. 2100 BC. The seated figure is probably king Ur-Nammu, bestowing the governorship on ·∏™a≈°·∏´amer, who is led before him by Lamma (protective goddess).[347]](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Sumerian_Cylinder_Seal_of_King_Ur-Nammu.jpg/250px-Sumerian_Cylinder_Seal_of_King_Ur-Nammu.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sumerian_Cylinder_Seal_of_King_Ur-Nammu.jpg)

[![Image 47: Luna on the Parabiago plate (2nd‚Äì5th century), featuring the crescent crown, chariot and velificatio as lunar aspect found in different cultures.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Patera_di_Parabiago_-_MI_-_Museo_archeologico_-_Diana_-_Luna_-_25-7-2003_-_Foto_Giovanni_Dall%27Orto_-_25-7-2003.jpg/250px-Patera_di_Parabiago_-_MI_-_Museo_archeologico_-_Diana_-_Luna_-_25-7-2003_-_Foto_Giovanni_Dall%27Orto_-_25-7-2003.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Patera_di_Parabiago_-_MI_-_Museo_archeologico_-_Diana_-_Luna_-_25-7-2003_-_Foto_Giovanni_Dall%27Orto_-_25-7-2003.jpg)

[![Image 48: Rabbits are in a range of cultures identified with the Moon, from China to the Indigenous peoples of the Americas, as with the rabbit (on the left) of the Maya moon goddess (6th‚Äì9th century).](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Goddess_O_Ixchel.jpg/250px-Goddess_O_Ixchel.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Goddess_O_Ixchel.jpg)

Humans have not only observed the Moon since [prehistoric times](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prehistoric_times "Prehistoric times"), but have also developed intricate perceptions of the Moon. Over time the Moon has been characterized and associated in many different ways, from having a [spirit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spirit_(vital_essence) "Spirit (vital essence)") or being [a deity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_deity "Lunar deity"), and an [aspect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aspect_(religion) "Aspect (religion)") thereof or an aspect [in astrology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon_(astrology) "Moon (astrology)"), being made an important part of many [cosmologies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cosmology "Cosmology").

This rich history of humans viewing the Moon has been evidenced starting with depictions from 40,000 [BP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Before_present "Before present") and in written form from the [4th millennium BCE](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/4th_millennium_BCE "4th millennium BCE") in the earliest cases of [writing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Writing "Writing"). The oldest named astronomer and poet [Enheduanna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enheduanna "Enheduanna"), [Akkadian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Akkadian_Empire "Akkadian Empire") high priestess to the lunar deity [Nanna/Sin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sin_(mythology) "Sin (mythology)") and pricess, daughter of [Sargon the Great](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sargon_the_Great "Sargon the Great") (c. 2334 ‚Äì c. 2279 BCE), tracked the Moon and wrote poems about her divine Moon.[[237]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-c099-250)

#### Crescent

For the representation of the Moon, especially its [lunar phases](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_phase "Lunar phase"), the [crescent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crescent "Crescent") (üåô) has been a recurring symbol in a range of cultures since at least 3,000 BCE or possibly earlier with bull horns dating to the earliest [cave paintings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cave_painting "Cave painting") at 40,000 [BP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Before_present "Before present").[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-e093-245)[[239]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-k874-252) In [writing systems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Writing_system "Writing system") such as Chinese the crescent has developed into the symbol [Êúà](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%9C%88 "wikt:Êúà"), the word for Moon, and in ancient Egyptian it was the symbol [ìáπ](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%F0%93%87%B9 "wikt:ìáπ"), meaning Moon and spelled like the ancient Egyptian lunar deity _[Iah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iah "Iah")_,[[348]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Hart_2005_p._77-361) which the other ancient Egyptian lunar deities [Khonsu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khonsu "Khonsu") and [Thoth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thoth "Thoth") were associated with.

Iconographically the crescent was used in [Mesopotamia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesopotamia "Mesopotamia") as the primary symbol of [Nanna/S√Æn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sin_(mythology) "Sin (mythology)"),[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-BlackGreen1992-249) the ancient [Sumerian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sumeria "Sumeria") lunar deity,[[349]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Nemet1998-362)[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-BlackGreen1992-249) who was the father of [Inanna/Ishtar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inanna "Inanna"), the goddess of the planet [Venus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus "Venus") (symbolized as the [eight pointed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Octagram "Octagram")[Star of Ishtar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Star_of_Ishtar "Star of Ishtar")),[[349]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Nemet1998-362)[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-BlackGreen1992-249) and [Utu/Shamash](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Utu "Utu"), the god of the Sun ([symbolized as a disc, optionally with eight rays](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_symbol "Solar symbol")),[[349]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Nemet1998-362)[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-BlackGreen1992-249) all three often depicted next to each other. Nanna/S√Æn is, like some other lunar deities, for example Iah and Khonsu of ancient Egypt, [Mene](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mene_(goddess) "Mene (goddess)")/[Selene](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Selene "Selene") of ancient Greece and [Luna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luna_(mythology) "Luna (mythology)") of ancient Rome, depicted as a [horned deity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Horned_deity "Horned deity"), featuring crescent shaped headgears or crowns.[[350]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-363)[[351]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-364)

The particular arrangement of the crescent with a star known as the [star and crescent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Star_and_crescent "Star and crescent") (‚ò™Ô∏è) goes back to the Bronze Age, representing either the Sun and Moon, or the Moon and the planet Venus, in combination. It came to represent the selene goddess [Artemis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis "Artemis"), and via the patronage of [Hecate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hecate "Hecate"), which as [triple deity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Triple_deity "Triple deity") under the [epithet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epithet "Epithet")_trimorphos_/_trivia_ included aspects of Artemis/[Diana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diana_(mythology) "Diana (mythology)"), came to be used as a [symbol of Byzantium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_flags_and_insignia "Byzantine flags and insignia"), with [Virgin Mary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Virgin_Mary "Virgin Mary") ([Queen of Heaven](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Queen_of_Heaven "Queen of Heaven")) later taking her place, becoming depicted in [Marian veneration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marian_veneration "Marian veneration") on a crescent and adorned with stars. Since then the [heraldric](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heraldry "Heraldry") use of the star and crescent proliferated, Byzantium's symbolism possibly influencing the development of the [Ottoman flag](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_flag "Ottoman flag"), specifically the combination of the Turkish crescent with a star,[[352]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-365) and becoming a popular [symbol for Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Symbols_of_Islam "Symbols of Islam") (as the _[hilal](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/hilal#Noun "wikt:hilal")_ of the [Islamic calendar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_calendar "Islamic calendar")) and [for a range of nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Star_and_crescent#Contemporary_use "Star and crescent").[[353]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Kadoi_2014-366)

#### Other associations

The features of the Moon, the contrasting brighter highlands and darker maria, have been seen by different cultures [forming abstract shapes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_pareidolia "Lunar pareidolia"). Such shapes are among others the [Man in the Moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Man_in_the_Moon "Man in the Moon") (e.g. [CoyolxƒÅuhqui](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coyolx%C4%81uhqui "CoyolxƒÅuhqui")) or the [Moon Rabbit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon_Rabbit "Moon Rabbit") (e.g. the Chinese [Tu'er Ye](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tu%27er_Ye "Tu'er Ye") or in [Indigenous American mythologies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mythologies_of_the_indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas "Mythologies of the indigenous peoples of the Americas") the aspect of the [Mayan Moon goddess](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maya_moon_goddess "Maya moon goddess"), from which possibly [Awilix](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Awilix "Awilix") is derived, or of [Metztli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metztli "Metztli")/[Tƒìcciztƒìcatl](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/T%C4%93ccizt%C4%93catl "Tƒìcciztƒìcatl")).[[347]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Collections_Search_%E2%80%93_Museum_of_Fine_Arts,_Boston_1987-360)

Occasionally some lunar deities have been also depicted [driving a chariot across the sky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luna_(goddess)#Chariot_of_the_Moon "Luna (goddess)"), such as the Hindu [Chandra/Soma](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chandra "Chandra"), the Greek Artemis, which is associated with Selene, or Luna, Selene's ancient Roman equivalent.

Color and material wise the Moon has been associated in Western [alchemy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alchemy "Alchemy") with [silver](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silver "Silver"), while gold is associated with the Sun.[[354]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Abbri_2019_pp._39%E2%80%9344-367)

Through a miracle, the so-called [splitting of the Moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Splitting_of_the_Moon "Splitting of the Moon") ([Arabic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic_language "Arabic language"): ÿßŸÜÿ¥ŸÇÿßŸÇ ÿßŸÑŸÇŸÖÿ±) in [Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam "Islam"), association with the Moon applies also to [Muhammad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad "Muhammad").[[355]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-368)

### Representation in modern culture

[![Image 49](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Van_Gogh_-_Starry_Night_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/250px-Van_Gogh_-_Starry_Night_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Van_Gogh_-_Starry_Night_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg)

[![Image 50](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Melies_color_Voyage_dans_la_lune.jpg/250px-Melies_color_Voyage_dans_la_lune.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Melies_color_Voyage_dans_la_lune.jpg)

The perception of the Moon in the [modern era](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_era "Modern era") has been informed by [telescope](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Telescope "Telescope")-enabled [modern astronomy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_astronomy "Modern astronomy") and later by [spaceflight](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spaceflight "Spaceflight") which enabled actual human activity at the Moon, particularly the [culturally impactful lunar landings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_program#Cultural_impact "Apollo program"). These new insights inspired cultural references, connecting romantic reflections about the Moon[[357]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-The_MIT_Press_Reader_2020-370) and speculative fiction such as science-fiction dealing with the Moon.[[356]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-The_New_York_Times_2019-369)[[358]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Nature_2019-371)

Contemporarily the Moon has been seen as a place for [economic expansion into space](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commercialization_of_space "Commercialization of space"), with missions prospecting for [lunar resources](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_resources "Lunar resources"). This has been accompanied with renewed public and critical reflection on humanity's cultural and [legal relation to the celestial body](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#Legal_status), especially regarding [colonialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonialism "Colonialism"),[[299]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Alvarez_2020_p.-312) as in the 1970 poem "[Whitey on the Moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Whitey_on_the_Moon "Whitey on the Moon")". In this light the Moon's nature has been invoked,[[330]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Declaration-343) particularly for lunar conservation[[301]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Nast_2013-314) and as a [common](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commons "Commons").[[359]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Open_Lunar_Foundation_2022-372)[[324]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-The_Space_Review_2021-337)[[332]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Evans_2021-345)

In 2021 20 July, the date of the [first crewed Moon landing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_11#Landing "Apollo 11"), became the annual _International Moon Day_.[[360]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-Nations_1967_a849-373)

### Lunar effect

The lunar effect is an unproven correlation between specific stages of the roughly 29.5-day lunar cycle and behavior and physiological changes in living beings on Earth, including humans. The Moon has long been associated with insanity and irrationality; the words _lunacy_ and _[lunatic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunatic "Lunatic")_ are derived from the Latin name for the Moon, _Luna_. Philosophers [Aristotle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aristotle "Aristotle") and [Pliny the Elder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pliny_the_Elder "Pliny the Elder") argued that the full moon induced insanity in susceptible individuals, believing that the brain, which is mostly water, must be affected by the Moon and its power over the tides, but the Moon's gravity is too slight to affect any single person.[[361]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-sciam-374) Even today, people who believe in a lunar effect claim that admissions to psychiatric hospitals, traffic accidents, homicides or suicides increase during a full moon,[[361]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-sciam-374) but over 37 studies invalidate these claims.[[362]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-RottonKelly1985-375) Lunar cycles have significant impacts on human culture but no solid evidence connects these cycles to human biology.[[363]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-FosterRoenneberg2008-376)

Explanatory notes
-----------------

1.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_ref-inclination_4-0)**Between 18.29¬∞ and 28.58¬∞ to Earth's [equator](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equator "Equator")[[1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-W06-1)
2.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_ref-near-Earth_asteroids_5-0)**There are a number of [near-Earth asteroids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Near-Earth_asteroid "Near-Earth asteroid"), including [3753 Cruithne](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/3753_Cruithne "3753 Cruithne"), that are [co-orbital](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Co-orbital "Co-orbital") with Earth: their orbits bring them close to Earth for periods of time but then alter in the long term (Morais et al, 2002). These are [quasi-satellites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quasi-satellite "Quasi-satellite")‚Äì they are not moons as they do not orbit Earth. For more information, see [Other moons of Earth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Other_moons_of_Earth "Other moons of Earth").
3.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_ref-maxval_18-0)**The _maximum value_ is given based on scaling of the brightness from the value of ‚àí12.74 given for an equator to Moon-centre distance of 378 000 km in the NASA factsheet reference to the minimum Earth‚ÄìMoon distance given there, after the latter is corrected for Earth's equatorial radius of 6 378 km, giving 350 600 km. The _minimum value_ (for a distant [new moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_moon "New moon")) is based on a similar scaling using the maximum Earth‚ÄìMoon distance of 407 000 km (given in the factsheet) and by calculating the brightness of the [earthshine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earthshine "Earthshine") onto such a new moon. The brightness of the earthshine is [ Earth [albedo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albedo "Albedo") √ó([Earth radius](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth_radius "Earth radius") / Radius of [Moon's orbit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon%27s_orbit "Moon's orbit"))2] relative to the direct solar illumination that occurs for a full moon. (Earth albedo = 0.367; Earth radius = (polar radius√ó equatorial radius)¬Ω = 6 367 km.)
4.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_ref-angular_size_20-0)**The range of angular size values given are based on simple scaling of the following values given in the fact sheet reference: at an Earth-equator to Moon-centre distance of 378 000 km, the [angular size](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Angular_size "Angular size") is 1896[arcseconds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arcsecond "Arcsecond"). The same fact sheet gives extreme Earth‚ÄìMoon distances of 407 000 km and 357 000 km. For the maximum angular size, the minimum distance has to be corrected for Earth's equatorial radius of 6 378 km, giving 350 600 km.
5.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_ref-pressure_explanation_22-0)**Lucey et al. (2006) give 10 7 particles cm‚àí3 by day and 10 5 particles cm‚àí3 by night. Along with equatorial surface temperatures of 390[K](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kelvin "Kelvin") by day and 100 K by night, the [ideal gas law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ideal_gas_law "Ideal gas law") yields the pressures given in the infobox (rounded to the nearest [order of magnitude](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Order_of_magnitude "Order of magnitude")): 10‚àí7[Pa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)") by day and 10‚àí10 Pa by night.
6.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_ref-23)**Because the Moon follows an elliptical path, its distance from Earth varies over the year, ranging from 357,000‚Äì407,000 kilometres (222,000‚Äì253,000 mi).[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_note-NASAfactsheet-2)
7.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_ref-71)**There is no strong correlation between the sizes of planets and the sizes of their satellites. Larger planets tend to have more satellites, both large and small, than smaller planets.
8.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_ref-Moon_vs._Charon_72-0)**With 27% the diameter and 60% the density of Earth, the Moon has 1.23% of the mass of Earth. The moon [Charon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charon_(moon) "Charon (moon)") is larger relative to its primary [Pluto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pluto "Pluto"), but Earth and the Moon are different since Pluto is considered a [dwarf planet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dwarf_planet "Dwarf planet") and not a planet, unlike Earth.
9.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_ref-orbpd_189-0)**More accurately, the Moon's mean sidereal period (fixed star to fixed star) is 27.321661 days (27 d 07 h 43 min 11.5 s), and its mean tropical orbital period (from equinox to equinox) is 27.321582 days (27 d 07 h 43 min 04.7 s) (_Explanatory Supplement to the Astronomical Ephemeris_, 1961, at p.107).
10.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_ref-synpd_190-0)**More accurately, the Moon's mean synodic period (between mean solar conjunctions) is 29.530589 days (29 d 12 h 44 min 02.9 s) (_Explanatory Supplement to the Astronomical Ephemeris_, 1961, at p.107).
11.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_ref-brightness_229-0)**The Sun's [apparent magnitude](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apparent_magnitude "Apparent magnitude") is ‚àí26.7, while the full moon's apparent magnitude is ‚àí12.7.
12.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_ref-size_changes_234-0)**See graph in [Sun#Life phases](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sun#Life_phases "Sun"). At present, the diameter of the Sun is increasing at a rate of about five percent per billion years. This is very similar to the rate at which the apparent angular diameter of the Moon is decreasing as it recedes from Earth.
13.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_ref-area_238-0)**On average, the Moon covers an area of 0.21078 square degrees on the night sky.

352.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon#cite_ref-365)**"It seems possible, though not certain, that after the conquest Mehmed took over the crescent _and_ star as an emblem of sovereignty from the Byzantines. The half-moon alone on a blood red flag, allegedly conferred on the Janissaries by Emir Orhan, was much older, as is demonstrated by numerous references to it dating from before 1453. But since these flags lack the star, which along with the half-moon is to be found on Sassanid and Byzantine municipal coins, it may be regarded as an innovation of Mehmed. It seems certain that in the interior of Asia tribes of Turkish nomads had been using the half-moon alone as an emblem for some time past, but it is equally certain that crescent and star _together_ are attested only for a much later period. There is good reason to believe that old Turkish and Byzantine traditions were combined in the emblem of Ottoman and, much later, present-day Republican Turkish sovereignty." Franz Babinger (William C. Hickman Ed., Ralph Manheim Trans.), _Mehmed the Conqueror and His Time_, Princeton University Press, 1992, p 108
